class=\"big-branded\">\n\n    <div class=\"publication-name\" id=\"wd-pub-name\">\n\t<div class=\"publication-title\" itemprop=\"name\" itemid=\"periodical\">\n\t\t\t\t<!-- Journal image link tile            <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">Discovery of a Lensed Ultrabright Submillimeter Galaxy at <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a02.0439</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">A. href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=11%2F18&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+high-redshift\">galaxies: high-redshift</a>; <a End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D2041-8205%2F843%2F2%2FL22\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">2041-8205/843/2/L22</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>We report an ultrabright lensed submillimeter galaxy (SMG) at <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a02.0439, <I>WISE</I> J132934.18+224327.3, identified as a result of a full-sky cross-correlation of the <I>AllWISE</I> and <I>Planck</I> compact source catalogs aimed to search for bright analogs of the SMG SMM J2135, the Cosmic Eyelash. Inspection of archival SCUBA-2 observations of the candidates revealed a source with fluxes (<IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${S}_{850\\mu {\\rm{m}}}=130$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/apjlaa79efieqn1.gif\"></IMG> mJy) consistent with the <I>Planck</I> measurements. The centroid of the SCUBA-2 source coincides within 1 arcsec with the position of the <I>AllWISE</I> mid-IR source, and, remarkably, with an arc-shaped lensed galaxy in <I>HST</I> images at visible wavelengths. Low-resolution rest-frame UV-optical spectroscopy of this lensed galaxy obtained with 10.4 m GTC reveals the typical absorption lines of a starburst galaxy. Gemini-N near-IR spectroscopy provided a clear detection of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${{\\rm{H}}}_{\\alpha }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/apjlaa79efieqn2.gif\"></IMG> emission. The lensed source appears to be gravitationally magnified by a massive foreground galaxy cluster lens at <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a00.44; modeling with Lenstool indicates a lensing amplification factor of 11\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02. We determine an intrinsic rest-frame 8\u20131000 <I>\u03bc</I>m luminosity, <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{IR}}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/apjlaa79efieqn3.gif\"></IMG>, of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$(1.3\\pm 0.1)\\times {10}^{13}\\,{L}_{\\odot }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/apjlaa79efieqn4.gif\"></IMG>, and a likely star formation rate (SFR) of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$\\sim 500\\mbox{--}2000\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/apjlaa79efieqn5.gif\"></IMG>. The SED shows a remarkable similarity with the Cosmic Eyelash from optical-mid/IR to submillimeter/radio, albeit at higher fluxes.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/843/2/L22&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/aa79ef&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/843/2/L22&doi=10.3847/2041-8213/aa79ef&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2017ApJ...843L..22D\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2017ApJ...843L..22D\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/2041-8205/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa79efs1\" name=\"apjlaa79efs1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Submillimeter galaxies (SMGs) provide important clues on the formation and evolution of massive galaxies in the distant universe (Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib4\">2014</a>). These high-<em>z</em> dusty starbursts, peaking at redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.3\u20132.5 (Chapman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib6\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib6\">2005</a>; Simpson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib38\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib38\">2014</a>; Strandet et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib42\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib42\">2016</a>) are massive and most probably the progenitors of present-day ellipticals (e.g., Ivison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib17\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib17\">2013</a>). Given the typical sizes of starbursts (less than a few kiloparsecs; e.g., Hodge et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib13\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib13\">2016</a>), even with ALMA and <em>HST</em> it is difficult to achieve the desirable spatial resolution to carry out detailed studies of star-forming regions in these dusty galaxies.</p><p>Strong gravitational lensing by massive galaxy clusters can enhance the apparent brightness of SMGs (Smail et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib41\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib41\">1997</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib40\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib40\">2002</a>). Wide <em>Herschel</em> surveys such as H-ATLAS, HerMES, or the south Pole Telescope and the <em>Planck</em> space mission provided an increasing number of bright lensed SMGs (Negrello et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib32\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib32\">2010</a>; Vieira et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib47\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib47\">2013</a>; Wei\u00df et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib50\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib50\">2013</a>; Ca\u00f1ameras et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib3\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib3\">2015</a>; Harrington et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib10\">2016</a>; Strandet et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib42\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib42\">2016</a>) that may allow their study at a resolution of 100 pc, close to the size of GMCs, and thus a better understanding of their ISM properties (see, e.g., Vlahakis et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib48\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib48\">2015</a>; Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib45\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib45\">2015</a>) and a comparison of them with galaxies in the local universe. Among SMGs, the serendipitously discovered lensed galaxy SMM J2135-0102 at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.3259 is outstanding (the Cosmic Eyelash Ivison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib18\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib18\">2010</a>; Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib44\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib44\">2010</a>; Danielson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib8\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib8\">2011</a>).</p><p>In this Letter, we present the first result of a search for the brightest examples in the sky of dusty star-forming high-redshift galaxies using data of the <em>Planck</em> and <em>WISE</em> space missions. We report the discovery of <em>WISE</em> J132934.18+224327.3 as a magnified SMG at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044 with spectral energy distribution (SED) remarkably similar to that of the Cosmic Eyelash but higher apparent brightness at all wavelengths from visible to radio. We adopt a flat \u039bCDM cosmology from Planck Collaboration XVI (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib35\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib35\">2014</a>) with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn6.gif\" alt=\"${H}_{0}=68$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{H}_{0}=68</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn7.gif\" alt=\"${}^{-1},{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{m}=0.31$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{}^{-1},{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{m}=0.31</script></span></span>, and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn8.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=1-{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{m}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}=1-{{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{m}</script></span></span>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa79efs2\" name=\"apjlaa79efs2\">2.\u00a0The Search</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>In order to find bright lensed SMGs in the full sky, we carried out a cross-matching between the <em>AllWISE</em><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn1\">5</a></sup>\n and <em>Planck</em><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn2\">6</a></sup>\n full-sky compact source catalogs. As a reference we adopted the SED of the Cosmic Eyelash (Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib44\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib44\">2010</a>), from the mid-infrared (MIR) to the submillimeter. Our aim was to identify candidates in these catalogs with MIR colors similar to the Cosmic Eyelash and strong submillimeter fluxes. First, we built a full-sky selection of galaxies verifying the color criteria <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn9.gif\" alt=\"$W1-W2\\gt 0.8,W2-W3\\lt 2.4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">W1-W2\\gt 0.8,W2-W3\\lt 2.4</script></span></span>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn10.gif\" alt=\"$W3-W4\\gt 3.5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">W3-W4\\gt 3.5</script></span></span> and detection at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn11.gif\" alt=\"$S/N\\gt 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">S/N\\gt 3</script></span></span> in the four bands of the <em>AllWISE</em> catalog; we limited the sample to galactic latitude <em>b</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn12.gif\" alt=\"$\\geqslant $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\geqslant</script></span></span> 20\u00b0. These color criteria were employed by Iglesias-Groth et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib15\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib15\">2017</a>) in their near-infrared (NIR)/MIR search for lensed SMGs. These criteria also select SMGs with SEDs similar to the average SED of 73 spectroscopically identified SMGs from Michalowski et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib29\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib29\">2010</a>), Hainline et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib9\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib9\">2011</a>), and to the ALESS SMG composite SED (Swinbank et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib46\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib46\">2014</a>). Only SMGs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn13.gif\" alt=\"$z=2-2.8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2-2.8</script></span></span> are expected to fulfill these color conditions.</p><p>Then, we requested the selected objects to have a <em>Planck</em> source detected within 5 arcmin with submillimeter flux ratios consistent with those expected for SMGs at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$z=2-3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2-3</script></span></span>. We found eight <em>WISE</em> candidates with SEDs consistent with the adopted references; however, the <em>Planck</em> submillimeter/millimeter maps for most of these sources clearly show contamination by galactic dust emission. Inspection of the <em>Planck</em> maps and available images from different optical and near-IR catalogs identified <em>WISE</em> J132934.18+224327.3 as the most likely counterpart of the submillimeter <em>Planck</em> source PCCS2 857 G007.94+80.29 and very promising candidate to an ultrabright SMG analog to the Cosmic Eyelash.</p><p>A subsequent search in CADC<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn3\">7</a></sup>\n provided detections by SCUBA-2 at James Clerk Maxwell Telescope of a submillimeter source with coordinates consistent within 1 arcsec with those of <em>WISE</em> J132934.18+224327.3, which could be responsible for the observed <em>Planck</em> submillimeter fluxes. In fact, the position of the source coincides with a strong lensing cluster SDSS 1329+2243 at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.44 (Bayliss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib1\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib1\">2014</a>), which has been observed by Jones (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib20\">2015</a>) with JCMT/SCUBA-2 and reported a source in snapshot observations at 850 and 450 <em>\u03bc</em>m with fluxes <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn15.gif\" alt=\"${S}_{450}\\approx 605$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{S}_{450}\\approx 605</script></span></span> mJy and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn16.gif\" alt=\"${S}_{850}\\approx 130$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{S}_{850}\\approx 130</script></span></span> mJy, consistent with being the main counterpart of the <em>Planck</em> source. Jones (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib20\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib20\">2015</a>) reported arc structures in Keck images suggesting it could be a lensed submillimeter source. Additional detections in the radio band are found in FIRST.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn4\">8</a></sup>\n\n</p><p>We used Vizier at CDS<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn5\">9</a></sup>\n to find the most likely counterpart of the <em>WISE/Planck/SCUBA-2</em> source in the near-IR and visible. In <em>HST-ACS</em><sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn6\">10</a></sup>\n images, a lensed galaxy is also detected at less than 1 arcsec of <em>WISE</em> J132934.18+224327.3. We postulate that this lensed galaxy is the optical counterpart of the strong submillimeter and mid-IR source (see Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff1\">1</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff2\">2</a>(a)). Hereafter, we designate this lensed galaxy as the \"Cosmic Eyebrow.\"</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa79eff1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa79eff1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79eff1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79eff1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0RGB image of the Cosmic Eyebrow with the <em>HST/WFC3</em> filters, blue F390W, green F606W, and red F160W. backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0(a) Imaging of the Cosmic Eyebrow with <em>HST</em> (left column), <em>WISE</em> (middle column), and SCUBA-2 (right column). The circles represent the counterpart of the <em>Planck</em> source in the related imaging. North is up; east is left. (b) GTC <em>g</em>-band imaging of the Cosmic Eyebrow. We show the orientation of the long slit (slit width of <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn17.gif\" alt=\"$0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8</script></span></span>) for our spectroscopic observations. North is up; east is left.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa79eff2\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa79eff2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa79eff2\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa79eff2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa79efs3\" name=\"apjlaa79efs3\">3.\u00a0Observations and Data Reduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjlaa79efs3-1\" name=\"apjlaa79efs3-1\">3.1.\u00a0GTC Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We have obtained spectroscopy of the lensed galaxy with the optical imager and spectrograph OSIRIS at the 10.4 m Gran Telescopio de Canarias (GTC), on the night of 2017 April 18 in clear conditions and dark moon with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn18.gif\" alt=\"$0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8</script></span></span> seeing. Observations were made using the low-resolution, long-slit mode with a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn19.gif\" alt=\"$0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 8</script></span></span> slit and the R500B grism. In this configuration, the resolution is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn20.gif\" alt=\"$R\\sim 540$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">R\\sim 540</script></span></span>, and we have 3.54 \u00c5 pix<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0from ~3700 to 7200 \u00c5. The slit was oriented along the line of the arc structure of the lensed source (PA of 64<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />22). We grouped observations in two observing blocks of two exposures of 1385 s each with a 60 s acquisition image per block in the <em>g</em> band (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff2\">2</a>). The seeing limited image shows an arc-like galaxy in the expected position for which we measured <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn21.gif\" alt=\"${g}_{\\mathrm{AB}}=22.85\\pm 0.03$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{g}_{\\mathrm{AB}}=22.85\\pm 0.03</script></span></span> for region 1 and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn22.gif\" alt=\"${g}_{\\mathrm{AB}}=23.43\\pm 0.04$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{g}_{\\mathrm{AB}}=23.43\\pm 0.04</script></span></span> for region 2. The spectroscopic observations, with a total integration time of 5540 s, were reduced using the noao/twodspec and noao/onedspec packages of IRAF to yield fluxed, wavelength-calibrated spectra. We extracted spectra for the full arc region along the slit and separately for encircled regions 1 and 2. Our GTC spectroscopy reveals that the two regions in the arc are the same source. In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff3\">3</a>, we show the individual spectra for each arc region and the total arc spectrum. The spectra of the two arc regions show strong absorption features. We derive the redshift from the fit of well-measured lines of Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn23.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1260.4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1260.4</script></span></span>, OI <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn24.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1302$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1302</script></span></span>, C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn25.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1334.5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1334.5</script></span></span>, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn26.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1526.7$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1526.7</script></span></span>, and Al <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn27.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1670.7$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1670.7</script></span></span>; for the full arc we find <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" 0.0004</script></span></span>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa79eff3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa79eff3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79eff3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0GTC/OSIRIS spectra of the two regions (up) and for the each individual regions (both downshifted for clarity). We mark the positions of the absorption features identified in the spectra. For comparison, we show the composite spectrum of LBGs from Shapley et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib37\">2003</a>). We also show in the inset the Gemini spectrum for region 1 and mark the emission lines we identify; the H<sub><em>\u03b1</em></sub> emission line yields a redshift for the source of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.0439.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjlaa79eff3\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/downloadFigure/figure/apjlaa79eff3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjlaa79eff3\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjlaa79eff3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa79efs3-2\" name=\"apjlaa79efs3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Gemini Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Archival GEMINI NIR-spectroscopic observations were found in CADC for region 1 of the arc. The spectrum was obtained using the cross-dispersed (XD) mode of the Gemini Near-IR Spectrograph on the 8.1 m Gemini-North telescope on the night of 2014 May 10 (under PI: Jane Rigby program ID: XGN-2014A-C-3) with the \"short blue\" camera, 32 l/mm grating and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn29.gif\" alt=\"$0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 68$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 68</script></span></span> slit. The slit used in this XD mode is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn30.gif\" alt=\"$7^{\\prime\\prime} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">7^{\\prime\\prime}</script></span></span> in length and the orientation was with a position angle (PA) of 89<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />7 in region 1. The telescope was nodded (typically <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn31.gif\" alt=\"$3\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">3\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 5</script></span></span> distant) in an ABBA-type pattern. We took the raw and calibration data from the CADC and reduced them using the Gemini IRAF package version v1.13.1 and following Mason et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib28\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib28\">2015</a>) and the instruction on the Reducing XD spectra webpage from GEMINI observatory.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn7\">11</a></sup>\n The total integration time for the spectrum was 3600 s, and two telluric stars of spectral type A0V were observed immediately before and after the galaxy. Only in the K band have we found useful data with a clear detection of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn32.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{H}}}_{\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{H}}}_{\\alpha }</script></span></span> in emission. In the inset of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff3\">3</a>, we show the spectrum near the H<sub><em>\u03b1</em></sub> emission line from which we obtain a redshift of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn33.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.0439\\pm 0.0006$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.0439\\pm 0.0006</script></span></span> in agreement with the rest-frame UV-spectrum. This redshift is consistent with the value published in Oguri et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib33\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib33\">2012</a>; <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn34.gif\" alt=\"$z\\approx 2.04$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\approx 2.04</script></span></span>) for a source coincident in position with the lensed galaxy.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa79efs4\" name=\"apjlaa79efs4\">4.\u00a0Analysis and Discussion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjlaa79efs4-1\" name=\"apjlaa79efs4-1\">4.1.\u00a0Lens Modeling</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We have used Lenstool<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn8\">12</a></sup>\n (Kneib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib25\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib25\">1993</a>; Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib21\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib21\">2007</a>) to perform a mass reconstruction of the foreground cluster, assuming a parametric model for the distribution of dark matter. This model was constrained using the location of the multiple images identified in the cluster. We used a simple model with a single cluster-scale mass component, as well as individual galaxy-scale mass components centered on each cluster member. For each component, we used a dual pseudo-isothermal elliptical mass distribution (dPIE, also known as a truncated PIEMD; Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib26\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib26\">2005</a>). Sextractor and visual inspection of the <em>HST/WFPC3</em> images provided an identification of six families of multiply lensed background galaxies, arclets with two to six components each, based on proximity, colors, and shape. The redshift of the family of the Cosmic Eyebrow (A in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff1\">1</a>) was fixed at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044, and for the other families was set as a free parameter. When modeling the lensing, the redshift of three families (B, C, and E in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff1\">1</a>) was found very close to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044, so we fixed it to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044 and for only two families were the redshifts considered a free parameter. We checked the model with the reconstruction of the arclets, and found good agreement between the positions for image arcs and the reconstruction of each component of the families. The data are best fitted with a cluster-scale potential of ellipticity <em>e</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.226, PA =\u00a047<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />00, and velocity dispersion <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn35.gif\" alt=\"${\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{PIEMD}}=830$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{PIEMD}}=830</script></span></span> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. The enclosed mass within an aperture of 250 kpc is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn36.gif\" alt=\"$M=1.8\\pm 0.5\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">M=1.8\\pm 0.5\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> with an Einstein radius of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn37.gif\" alt=\"${\\theta }_{{\\rm{e}}}=11.\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\theta }_{{\\rm{e}}}=11.\\,\\pm \\,0\\buildrel{\\prime\\prime}\\over{.} 4</script></span></span> at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044. The amplification is obtained from the comparison between the main characteristic of the galaxies in the source plane and in the image plane; we find an amplification factor of 11\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02 for the two main members of the Cosmic Eyebrow family, which are our spectroscopy regions on the arc indicated in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff2\">2</a>. The mean amplification factors for each family with <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.044 are <em>A</em>\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn38.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,11\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,11\\pm 2</script></span></span>, <em>B</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn39.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,7\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,7\\pm 2</script></span></span>, <em>C</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn40.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,14\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,14\\pm 2</script></span></span>, and <em>E</em>\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn41.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,7\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,7\\pm 2</script></span></span>. The largest amplification is for the brightest member of family <em>C</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn42.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,20\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,20\\pm 2</script></span></span>; for the other two families the mean amplification factors are <em>D</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn43.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,4\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,4\\pm 2</script></span></span> (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn44.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 2.9$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 2.9</script></span></span>) and <em>F</em> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn45.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim \\,5\\pm 2$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim \\,5\\pm 2</script></span></span> (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn46.gif\" alt=\"$z\\sim 1.0$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\sim 1.0</script></span></span>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa79efs4-2\" name=\"apjlaa79efs4-2\">4.2.\u00a0SED</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We plot the SED (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff4\">4</a>) assuming the lensed source in the <em>HST</em> and GTC images is the counterpart of the SCUBA-2 and <em>WISE</em> detections (all positions coincident within 1 arcsec) and list the photometry data in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjlaa79eft1\">1</a>. We calculate the upper limit for the <em>K</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> and <em>H</em> bands from the UKIDSS catalog<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn9\">13</a></sup>\n and for 60 and 100 <em>\u03bc</em>m from the <em>IRAS</em> Sky Survey Atlas.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjlaa79effn10\">14</a></sup>\n This SED is consistent with a source at redshift <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn47.gif\" alt=\"$z=2-2.5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2-2.5</script></span></span>, and as expected, it is very well fitted by the SED of the Cosmic Eyelash in that redshift range. At all frequencies from optical to radio, the Cosmic Eyebrow is brighter than the Cosmic Eyelash.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjlaa79eff4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjlaa79eff4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79eff4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79eff4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Multi-wavelength spectral energy distribution of the Cosmic Eyebrow. class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/suppdata/apjlaa79eft1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/2041-8213/aa79ef\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/843/2/L22/suppdata/apjlaa79eft1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We calculate the rest-frame 8\u20131000 <em>\u03bc</em>m luminosity, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn48.gif\" alt=\"${L}_{\\mathrm{IR}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{L}_{\\mathrm{IR}}</script></span></span>, from direct integration of the data fit, and obtain an intrinsic luminosity for our galaxy <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn49.gif\" alt=\"$L(\\mathrm{Eyebrow})=(1.3\\pm 0.1)\\times {10}^{13}\\,{L}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">L(\\mathrm{Eyebrow})=(1.3\\pm 0.1)\\times {10}^{13}\\,{L}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, indicating an SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn50.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 2000\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 2000\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span> (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib22\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib22\">1998</a>), which assumes a Salpeter IMF, assuming a Chabrier IMF would possibly be a factor of ~1.8 lower (Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib4\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib4\">2014</a>).</p><p>We also use the MAGPHYS code that allows us to fit simultaneously the ultraviolet-to-radio SED, so we can constrain physical parameters (Da Cunha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib7\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib7\">2015</a>). The fit is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjlaa79eff4\">4</a>; we would benefit from measurements in photometric bands between 22 and 350 <em>\u03bc</em>m in order to establish which SED better describes the Cosmic Eyebrow. From this fit we give the median-likelihood estimates (and confidence ranges) of several physical parameters corrected for lensing amplification, stellar mass <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn51.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({M}_{* }/{M}_{\\odot })={11.49}_{-0.05}^{+0.06}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({M}_{* }/{M}_{\\odot })={11.49}_{-0.05}^{+0.06}</script></span></span>, star formation rate <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn52.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}(\\mathrm{SFR}/{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})={2.73}_{-0.01}^{+0.02}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}(\\mathrm{SFR}/{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})={2.73}_{-0.01}^{+0.02}</script></span></span>, mass-weighted age <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn53.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({\\mathrm{age}}_{M}\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})={9.28}_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({\\mathrm{age}}_{M}\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1})={9.28}_{-0.01}^{+0.01}</script></span></span>, average V-band dust attenuation <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn54.gif\" alt=\"${A}_{V}={3.30}_{-0.02}^{+0.02}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{A}_{V}={3.30}_{-0.02}^{+0.02}</script></span></span>, H-band mass-to-light ratio <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn55.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({M}_{* }/{L}_{H})\\,={0.14}_{-0.01}^{+0.01}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({M}_{* }/{L}_{H})\\,={0.14}_{-0.01}^{+0.01}</script></span></span>, total dust luminosity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn56.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({L}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/{L}_{\\odot })={13.27}_{-0.02}^{+0.01}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({L}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/{L}_{\\odot })={13.27}_{-0.02}^{+0.01}</script></span></span>, luminosity-averaged dust temperature <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn57.gif\" alt=\"${T}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/K={40}_{-2}^{+7}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{T}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/K={40}_{-2}^{+7}</script></span></span>, and total dust mass <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn58.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({M}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/{M}_{\\odot })={9.19}_{-0.08}^{+0.15}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({M}_{\\mathrm{dust}}/{M}_{\\odot })={9.19}_{-0.08}^{+0.15}</script></span></span>. These physical parameters compare well with the average properties of the ALESS SMGs in Da Cunha et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib7\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib7\">2015</a>). The SFR obtained with MAGPHYS is lower than estimated with the Kennicutt (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib22\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib22\">1998</a>) relation. This is partially due to the use of the Chabrier IMF and to the additional dust heating caused by the relatively old stellar populations of our galaxy that increases the dust luminosity at fixed SFRs (Da Cunha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib7\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib7\">2015</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjlaa79efs4-3\" name=\"apjlaa79efs4-3\">4.3.\u00a0Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The UV rest-frame spectrum of the Cosmic Eyebrow resembles that of Lyman break galaxies (LBGs; Shapley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib37\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib37\">2003</a>) and displays the strong interstellar absorption features typical of the spectra of starburst galaxies (Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib5\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib5\">2013</a>). We identify in the observed spectrum low-ionization resonance interstellar metal lines such as Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn59.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1260.4$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1260.4</script></span></span>, OI 1302 Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn60.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1304$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1304</script></span></span>, C <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn61.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1334$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1334</script></span></span>, Si <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn62.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1526$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1526</script></span></span>, and Al <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn63.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1670$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1670</script></span></span> that are associated with the neutral interstellar medium. We also detect high-ionization metal lines of Si <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn64.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda \\lambda 1393,1402$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda \\lambda 1393,1402</script></span></span> and C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn65.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda \\lambda 1548,1550$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda \\lambda 1548,1550</script></span></span> that are associated with ionized interstellar gas and PCygni stellar wind features. The C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> feature exhibits a strong interstellar absorption component plus a weaker blueshifted broad absorption and marginal evidence of redshifted emission associated with stellar winds that likely originate in main-sequence, giant, and supergiant O stars (Walborn &amp; Panek <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib49\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib49\">1984</a>). Our data do not show evidence for the He <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn66.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 1640$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 1640</script></span></span>, which could be an indication of a low ratio of Wolf\u2013Rayet to O stars (Schaerer &amp; Vacca <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib36\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib36\">1998</a>).</p><p>In the spectrum of the region 1 of the arc, we find H<sub><em>\u03b1</em></sub> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn67.gif\" alt=\"$19982\\pm 4\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">19982\\pm 4\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> and the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn68.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 6583$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 6583</script></span></span> at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn69.gif\" alt=\"$20041\\pm 5\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">20041\\pm 5\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span>. Full width at half maximum (FWHM) line widths are 386\u00a0\u00b1\u00a020 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> and 331\u00a0\u00b1\u00a020 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>; after correction for the instrumental profile, we estimate that the intrinsic width of these lines is 150\u00a0\u00b1\u00a025 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. The low [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn70.gif\" alt=\"$\\lambda 6583$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\lambda 6583</script></span></span>/H<sub><em>\u03b1</em></sub> ratio of 0.33\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04 suggests a star-forming region (Kewley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib23\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib23\">2013</a>). The EW<sub>rest</sub> (H<sub><em>\u03b1</em></sub>)\u00a0=\u00a0<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn71.gif\" alt=\"$111\\pm 10\\,\\mathring{\\rm A} $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">111\\pm 10\\,\\mathring{\\rm A}</script></span></span> compares well with values reported in other well-known SMGs of a similar luminosity (Olivares et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjlaa79efbib34\" id=\"fnref-apjlaa79efbib34\">2016</a>).</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjlaa79efs5\" name=\"apjlaa79efs5\">5.\u00a0Conclusions</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>A cross-match of the <em>AllWISE</em> and <em>Planck</em> compact source catalogs aimed to identify the brightest examples of SMGs in the full-sky uncovered <em>WISE</em> J132934.18+224327.3, the Cosmic Eyebrow, a <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn72.gif\" alt=\"$z=2.0439\\pm 0.0006$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z=2.0439\\pm 0.0006</script></span></span> galaxy with a spectral energy distribution from mid-IR to submillimeter similar to that of the Cosmic Eyelash and higher observed fluxes. Archival data of SCUBA-2 and <em>HST</em> reveal a multiple lensed galaxy at the position of the strong submillimeter source. Follow-up observations with GTC/OSIRIS provided a precise redshift determination of the lensed galaxy and a rest-frame UV-spectrum with clearly identified low-ionization resonance interstellar metal lines that is consistent with that of starburst galaxies. Near-IR spectroscopy with Gemini-North showed <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn73.gif\" alt=\"${{\\rm{H}}}_{\\alpha }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{{\\rm{H}}}_{\\alpha }</script></span></span> in emission at a strength consistent with values reported for other SMGs. This galaxy is gravitationally magnified by a massive cluster at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.44; modeling with Lenstool indicates a lensing amplification factor of 11\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02. The intrinsic rest-frame 8\u20131000 <em>\u03bc</em>m luminosity of the lensed galaxy is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn74.gif\" alt=\"$(1.3\\pm 0.1)\\times {10}^{13}\\,{L}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">(1.3\\pm 0.1)\\times {10}^{13}\\,{L}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> indicating a likely SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/843/2/L22/Full/apjlaa79efieqn75.gif\" alt=\"$\\sim 500\\mbox{--}2000\\,{M}_{\\odot }{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sim 500\\mbox{--}2000\\,{M}_{\\odot }{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>. The SED of this new SMG resembles the Cosmic Eyelash from optical/mid-IR to submillimeter/radio, albeit at higher intrinsic luminosity. It is one of the brightest examples of SMGs so far reported, which may enable detailed high spatial resolution studies of star-forming regions in such dusty galaxies.</p></div> <div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Based on observations made with the GTC telescope, in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrof\u00edsica de Canarias. This work has been partially funded by projects ESP2015-69020-C2-1-R, ESP2014-56869-C2-2-P, and AYA2015-69350-C3-3-P (MINECO). H.D. acknowledges financial support from the Spanish Ministry of Economy and Competitiveness (MINECO) under the 2014 Ram\u00f3n y Cajal program MINECO RYC-2014-15686. We thank David Valls-Gabaud for his suggestions and comments on various aspects of this work. We are grateful to the anonymous referee for useful comments on the Letter.</p></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">Discovery of a Lensed Ultrabright Submillimeter Galaxy at <I>z</I>\u00a0=\u00a02.0439</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">A. Dimensions display -->\n<!-- End Dimensions display -->\n        <div class=\"clear-fl\"></div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Start MathJax links -->\n\t\t<div>\n\t\t  <a href=\"#\" id=\"mathJaxOff\"
